# Task: Kubelet Container Manager Architecture Guide

**Repository:** kubernetes/kubernetes (stripped snapshot)
**Output:** Write your document to `/workspace/documentation.md`

## Objective

Produce a subsystem architecture guide for kubelet container manager, including resource manager interactions and platform variance.

## Scope

Focus on the kubelet container manager subsystem.
Your document must explain component responsibilities, end-to-end flow, and extension or operational tradeoffs.

## Content Expectations

Address all of the following in your own structure:
- subsystem purpose, boundaries, and upstream/downstream dependencies
- key components and how responsibilities are split
- end-to-end control/request flow with concrete repository evidence
- failure modes, limits, and design tradeoffs
- extension points, customization hooks, and associated risks
- a concise map of the most important files/directories used in your analysis

## Quality Bar

- Cite concrete file paths from the repository.
- Explain behavior and interactions, not just API signatures.
- Include at least one section on operational implications (performance, reliability, or maintainability).
- Do not fabricate classes, functions, or files.

## Anti-Requirements

- Do not output `doc.go`.
- Do not provide shallow bullet dumps without system flow explanation.
- Do not rely on external docs not present in the workspace.

I am thinking...: I now have enough information to write a comprehensive architecture guide. Let me organize what I know:

1. **Top-level interface**: `ContainerManager` (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:66)
   - Linux impl: `containerManagerImpl` (pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go:100)
   - Windows impl: partial implementation in container_manager_windows.go
   - Stub/noop: container_manager_stub.go (test use), container_manager_unsupported.go (!linux && !windows)

2. **Cgroup layer**:
   - `CgroupManager` interface (pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go:64)
   - `CgroupName` = []string abstract path (types.go:49)
   - `CgroupConfig` holds Name + ResourceParameters (types.go:55)
   - `ResourceConfig` (types.go:27): Memory, CPUSet, CPUShares, CPUQuota, CPUPeriod, HugePageLimit, PidsLimit, Unified
   - Factory: `NewCgroupManager()` in cgroup_manager_linux.go:155 - dispatches to v1 or v2
   - v1: `cgroupV1impl` (cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go)
   - v2: `cgroupV2impl` (cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go)
   - Both extend `cgroupCommon` which uses `libcontainercgroups` (opencontainers/cgroups)
   - Driver modes: cgroupfs vs systemd (CgroupName.ToSystemd() vs ToCgroupfs())
   - CgroupName conversion: {"kubepods","burstable","podXXX"} -> /kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-podXXX.slice

3. **Cgroup hierarchy** (Linux):
   - `kubepods` (Node Allocatable root, aka cgroupRoot)
     - `kubepods/burstable` (Burstable QoS tier)
       - `kubepods/burstable/podUID` (pod cgroup)
         - container cgroups (managed by CRI)
     - `kubepods/besteffort` (BestEffort QoS tier)
       - `kubepods/besteffort/podUID`
     - `kubepods/podUID` (Guaranteed pods go directly under root)
   - System reserved cgroup (optional): user-specified
   - Kube reserved cgroup (optional): user-sp

Initially this contains all CPU IDs on the system. As\n    84  //     exclusive allocations are created and destroyed, this CPU set shrinks\n    85  //     and grows, accordingly. This is stored in the state as the default\n    86  //     CPU set.\n    87  //\n    88  //   - RESERVED: A subset of the shared pool which is not exclusively\n    89  //     allocatable. The size of the reserved pool is\n    91  //     ceil(systemreserved.cpu + kubereserved.cpu).\n    92  //     Reserved CPUs are taken topologically starting with lowest-indexed\n    93  //     physical core, as reported by cAdvisor.\n    94  //\n    95  //   - ASSIGNABLE: Equal to SHARED - RESERVED. 63  func MilliCPUToQuota(milliCPU int64, period int64) (quota int64) {\n    64          // CFS quota is measured in two values:\n    65          //  - cfs_period_us=100ms (the amount of time to "350  func (m *manager) GetAllCPUs() cpuset.CPUSet {\n   351          return m.allCPUs.Clone()\n   352  }\n   353\n   354  type reconciledContainer struct {\n   355          podName       string\n   356          containerName string\n   357          containerID   string\n   358  }\n   359\n   360  func (m *manager) removeStaleState(rootLogger logr.Logger) {\n   361          // Only once all sources are ready do we attempt to remove any stale state.\n   362          // This ensures that the call to `m.activePods()` below will succeed with\n   363          // the actual active pods list.\n   364          if !m.sourcesReady.AllReady() {\n   365                  return\n   366          }\n   367\n   368          // We grab the lock to ensure that no new containers will grab CPUs while\n   369          // executing the code below. It targets engineers who need to understand, debug, or extend\nthe subsystem. All file paths are relative to the repository root. All symbols cited\nexist in the source at the commit that was read to produce this document.\n\n---\n\n## Table of Contents\n\n1. [Scope and Purpose](#1-scope-and-purpose)\n2. [Platform Variants](#9-platform-variants)\n10. [File Map](#10-file-map)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Scope and Purpose\n\nThe container manager subsystem sits between the kubelet's pod-sync logic and the\nLinux kernel's resource controls. Its responsibilities divide into three layers:\n\n1. **Node-level resource accounting** \u2013 computing how much CPU, memory, and storage is\n   actually allocatable after reservations, and enforcing those limits via cgroups.\n2. **Per-pod and per-container isolation** \u2013 creating and tearing down the cgroup tree\n   that corresponds to each pod's QoS class and each container within it.\n3. **Extended resource management** \u2013 admitting and accounting for hardware devices\n   (device plugins), dynamic resource allocations (DRA/ResourceClaims), CPU pinning,\n   NUMA-local memory allocation, and cross-resource NUMA alignment.\n\nNothing in this subsystem communicates directly with the container runtime for normal\nI/O operations. Its only CRI interaction is calling `UpdateContainerResources` from the\nCPU manager's reconcile loop (and the memory manager) to push cpuset / memory node\nconstraints into already-running containers.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Top-Level Interface and Implementations\n\n```\npkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go  \u2013 ContainerManager interface (line 66)\n```\n\n`ContainerManager` is the fa\u00e7ade the rest of the kubelet uses. Key methods:\n\n| Method | Caller | Purpose |\n|--------|--------|---------|\n| `Start()` | `kubelet.go:1752` | Initialises all sub-managers, builds cgroup tree |\n| `NewPodContainerManager()` | `kubelet_pods.go:621`, `kubelet.go:2052` | Factory for per-pod cgroup operations |\n| `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` | `kubelet.go:1064` | Returns topology manager as PodAdmitHandler |\n| `UpdatePluginResources()` | `kubelet.go:1067` | Device plugin Allocate at admission |\n| `GetResources()` | `kubelet_pods.go:632` | Collects device/DRA run options for CRI |\n| `PrepareDynamicResources()` | `kubelet.go:3310` | Calls DRA NodePrepareResources before pod starts |\n| `UnprepareDynamicResources()` | `kubelet.go:3316` | Calls DRA NodeUnprepareResources after pod stops |\n| `UpdateQOSCgroups()` | `kubelet.go:2102` | Re-reconciles QoS CPU shares during syncPod |\n| `InternalContainerLifecycle()` | various | Returns the pre-create/pre-start/post-stop hook handler |\n| `Updates()` | `kubelet.go:2669` | Channel carrying device/DRA health-status change events |\n\n**Linux implementation**: `containerManagerImpl` (line 100 of\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go`). Its fields are the union of all\nsub-managers:\n\n```go\ntype containerManagerImpl struct {\n    NodeConfig\n    cgroupManager       CgroupManager\n    qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n    cpuManager          cpumanager.Manager\n    memoryManager       memorymanager.Manager\n    deviceManager       devicemanager.Manager  // interface\n    draManager          *dra.Manager\n    topologyManager     topologymanager.Manager\n    // cgroup root name, capacity, internalCapacity, subsystems, \u2026\n}\n```\n\n`containerManagerImpl` itself never writes cgroup files directly \u2013 all cgroup I/O is\ndelegated to `cgroupManager`.\n\n**Construction**: `NewContainerManager()` (`container_manager_linux.go`) is called from\n`cmd/kubelet/app/server.go`. The construction order matters: topology manager is\ncreated first so that `deviceManager`, `cpuManager`, and `memoryManager` can each call\n`AddHintProvider(logger, <self>)` to register as hint sources.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Component Responsibilities\n\n### 3.1 CgroupManager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` (interface), `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go`\n(shared helpers + factory), `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`\n\nThe `CgroupManager` interface (`types.go:64`) provides Create / Destroy / Update /\nExists / Validate / Pids / MemoryUsage / GetCgroupConfig / SetCgroupConfig. There are\ntwo concrete implementations:\n\n- `cgroupV1impl` \u2013 cgroup v1, uses per-controller directories under\n  `/sys/fs/cgroup/{cpu,memory,pids,\u2026}`.\n- `cgroupV2impl` \u2013 cgroup v2, unified hierarchy under `/sys/fs/cgroup/`.\n\nBoth embed `cgroupCommon` which holds the `CgroupSubsystems` mount map and the\n`useSystemd` flag.  All cgroup I/O is delegated to\n`github.com/opencontainers/cgroups/manager`, the same library used by containerd/runc.\n\nThe factory `NewCgroupManager()` (`cgroup_manager_linux.go:155`) decides which\nimplementation to construct by calling `libcontainercgroups.IsCgroup2UnifiedMode()`.\n\n`ResourceConfig` (`types.go:27`) is the platform-neutral description of cgroup\nparameters:\n\n| Field | v1 file | v2 file |\n|-------|---------|---------|\n| `Memory *int64` | `memory.limit_in_bytes` | `memory.max` |\n| `CPUShares *uint64` | `cpu.shares` | `cpu.weight` (scaled) |\n| `CPUQuota *int64` + `CPUPeriod *uint64` | `cpu.cfs_quota_us` / `cpu.cfs_period_us` | `cpu.max` (combined) |\n| `CPUSet cpuset.CPUSet` | `cpuset.cpus` | `cpuset.cpus` |\n| `PidsLimit *int64` | `pids.max` | `pids.max` |\n| `HugePageLimit map[int64]int64` | `hugetlb.<sz>.limit_in_bytes` | `hugetlb.<sz>.max` |\n| `Unified map[string]string` | \u2013 | arbitrary v2 key/value (e.g., `memory.min`, `memory.high`) |\n\n**Conversion helpers** (`helpers_linux.go`):\n\n- `MilliCPUToShares(milliCPU int64) uint64` \u2013 maps milliCPU to `cpu.shares` in the\n  range [2, 262144], at 1024 shares per CPU.\n- `MilliCPUToQuota(milliCPU int64, period int64) int64` \u2013 produces CFS quota\n  microseconds. Minimum quota is 1 ms (MinQuotaPeriod = 1000 \u00b5s).\n- `ResourceConfigForPod()` \u2013 sums all container requests/limits in a pod and produces\n  a `ResourceConfig` for the pod-level cgroup.\n\n### 3.2 Node Allocatable enforcement\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/node_container_manager_linux.go`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/helpers_linux.go` (NodeAllocatableRoot, GetCgroupSubsystems)\n\nNode Allocatable is the amount of compute capacity the scheduler uses. Its value is:\n\n```\nAllocatable = capacity \u2212 systemReserved \u2212 kubeReserved \u2212 evictionThreshold\n```\n\n`evictionThreshold` is derived from `hardEvictionReservation()` (`helpers.go:43`),\nwhich inspects `HardEvictionThresholds` for `memory` and `ephemeral-storage` signals.\n\n`createNodeAllocatableCgroups()` creates the top-level `kubepods` cgroup (the value of\n`NodeConfig.CgroupRoot`, default `\"kubepods\"`, line 39 of\n`node_container_manager_linux.go`). If enforcement is enabled, it uses `internalCapacity`\n(capacity minus reservations) as the cgroup resource limit.\n\n`enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()` writes limits onto the `kubepods` cgroup.  Because\nexisting pods may already exceed the target memory limit at enforcement time (for\nexample on a live node whose reservations just increased), the update is retried in a\nbackground goroutine that loops with a one-minute sleep until success. The system emits\na `SuccessfulNodeAllocatableEnforcement` event on success and\n`FailedNodeAllocatableEnforcement` on each failure.\n\nOptionally, `EnforceNodeAllocatable` can also apply limits to the user-configured\nsystem-reserved and kube-reserved cgroups (`nc.SystemReservedCgroupName`,\n`nc.KubeReservedCgroupName`).\n\n`setupNode()` (`container_manager_linux.go:504`) sequences the setup:\n1. Validate system requirements (cgroup mounts, etc.).\n2. Check / modify kernel tunables via `setupKernelTunables()`:\n   - `vm.overcommit_memory = 1` (always)\n   - `vm.panic_on_oom = 0` (invoke OOM killer, not panic)\n   - `kernel.panic = 10` (reboot after 10 s)\n   - `kernel.panic_on_oops = 1`\n   - `kernel.keys.root_maxkeys` / `root_maxbytes`\n   - Behaviour is `warn`, `error`, or `modify` depending on `ProtectKernelDefaults`.\n3. Create node allocatable cgroups.\n4. Start QoS container manager.\n5. Enforce node allocatable cgroup limits.\n6. Optionally place the kubelet process itself in `KubeletCgroupsName`.\n\n### 3.3 QOSContainerManager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`\n\nThe QoS container manager owns the two intermediate cgroup tiers \u2013\n`kubepods/burstable` and `kubepods/besteffort` \u2013 created during `Start()`. The\nGuaranteed tier is represented by `kubepods` itself (the cgroup root for pods):\n\n```go\nm.qosContainersInfo = QOSContainersInfo{\n    Guaranteed: rootContainer,                         // kubepods\n    Burstable:  NewCgroupName(rootContainer, \"burstable\"),\n    BestEffort: NewCgroupName(rootContainer, \"besteffort\"),\n}\n```\n\nIts sole ongoing job is `UpdateCgroups()`, called:\n\n- Once at startup.\n- Every `periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval` (1 minute, line 45) via a goroutine started\n  in `Start()`.\n- Synchronously during `syncPod` via `containerManager.UpdateQOSCgroups()`.\n\n`UpdateCgroups()` performs two adjustments:\n\n1. **CPU shares** (`setCPUCgroupConfig()`): sums the CPU requests of all currently\n   active Burstable pods, translates to CFS shares with `MilliCPUToShares()`, and\n   writes the result to `kubepods/burstable`. BestEffort is pinned to MinShares (2).\n2. **Memory reservation** (`setMemoryReserve()`): if `--qos-reserved memory=X%` is\n   set, derives per-tier memory limits from the formula\n   `burstableLimit = allocatable \u2212 (guaranteedRequests \u00d7 X%)`; the BestEffort limit is\n   further reduced.\n3. **MemoryQoS** (`setMemoryQoS()`): if the `MemoryQoS` feature gate and cgroup v2 are\n   both active, sets `memory.min` on the QoS tiers via the `Unified` map to provide\n   under-pressure memory protection for requests.\n\n### 3.4 PodContainerManager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` (interface), `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go`\n\n`PodContainerManager` is a per-use-site factory product: kubelet calls\n`containerManager.NewPodContainerManager()` wherever it needs to manipulate a pod's\ncgroup. This returns `podContainerManagerImpl` when `CgroupsPerQOS=true`, or a no-op\n`podContainerManagerNoop` otherwise.\n\n`GetPodContainerName(*v1.Pod)` maps a pod to its cgroup path. The path is:\n\n```\n<qosTierCgroupName> / pod<UID-with-dashes-escaped>\n```\n\nFor a Guaranteed pod:  `kubepods/pod<UID>`\nFor a Burstable pod:   `kubepods/burstable/pod<UID>`\nFor a BestEffort pod:  `kubepods/besteffort/pod<UID>`\n\n`EnsureExists()` creates the cgroup if absent, computing resource limits with\n`ResourceConfigForPod()`. The `DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs` feature gate\n(`kubefeatures.DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs`) suppresses CFS quota if any\ncontainer in the pod already has exclusive CPUs assigned by the CPU manager.\n\n`ReduceCPULimits()` sets CPU quota to the minimum before destruction, preventing new\nprocesses from accumulating CPU credit while the cgroup is being drained.\n\n`tryKillingCgroupProcesses()` is called on pod teardown. It enumerates the PIDs in\nthe pod cgroup via `CgroupManager.Pids()` and kills them, retrying up to five times.\n\n### 3.5 CPU Manager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` (Manager interface + manager struct),\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go` (Policy interface),\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_static.go` (staticPolicy),\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_none.go`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_options.go` (StaticPolicyOptions),\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/topology/` (CPU topology discovery),\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/state/` (state persistence)\n\n**Model**: the static policy partitions the machine's logical CPUs into three sets:\n\n- **Reserved** (`RESERVED`): CPUs carved off to satisfy `systemReserved.cpu +\n  kubeReserved.cpu`. Their count is `\u2308reservedCPUsFloat\u2309`.  By default these\n  CPUs remain available for the shared pool; with `strict-cpu-reservation=true`\n  they are fully removed from allocation.\n- **Shared** (default pool, informally `SHARED`): CPUs used by containers that have\n  not requested exclusive allocation (best-effort, burstable, or guaranteed with\n  non-integer CPU limits).\n- **Exclusive** (`EXCLUSIVE`): CPUs pinned to a specific container. Only Guaranteed\n  pods whose CPU request is a positive integer and whose limit equals the request\n  qualify. The static policy checks `GetAllocatableCPUs()` to find available CPUs and\n  writes the assignment into the persistent state.\n\n**Allocation path** (called from topology manager during admission):\n\n```\ntopologyManager.Admit()\n  \u2192 HintProvider.Allocate(pod, container)  [cpuManager implements HintProvider]\n  \u2192 cpuManager.Allocate(pod, container)\n    \u2192 policy.Allocate(logger, state, pod, container)\n```\n\n`Allocate()` first calls `removeStaleState()` (garbage-collects entries whose pods are\nno longer active), then delegates to `policy.Allocate()`, which records the assignment\nin the in-memory and checkpointed state.\n\n**Reconcile loop** (`reconcileState()`, started by `Start()` at\n`cpu_manager.go:255`): runs every `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod` (default 10 s). For\nevery running container it reads the stored cpuset and calls\n`updateContainerCPUSet()` \u2192 CRI `UpdateContainerResources`. This closes the gap\nbetween state changes that happen while a container is already running (e.g., init\ncontainer exits, reserved CPUs recalculated, kubelet restart).\n\n**State persistence**: `state.NewCheckpointState()` reads and writes\n`{KubeletRootDir}/cpu_manager_state`. The file contains a JSON map of\n`(podUID, containerName) \u2192 CPUSet`. On first start with `static` policy, if the\ncheckpoint file contains assignments from a different policy, startup fails (safe\ndefault\u2014operator must drain the node and delete the state file).\n\n**Policy options** (configured via `--cpu-manager-policy-options` on the kubelet):\n\n| Option | Stability | Behaviour |\n|--------|-----------|-----------|\n| `full-pcpus-only` | stable | Only allocate complete physical CPUs (both hyperthreads together) |\n| `strict-cpu-reservation` | stable | Remove reserved CPUs from the allocatable pool entirely |\n| `distribute-cpus-across-numa` | beta | Spread exclusive CPUs evenly across NUMA nodes when multiple nodes are required |\n| `prefer-align-cpus-by-uncorecache` | beta | Best-effort alignment to uncore cache boundaries |\n| `align-by-socket` | alpha | Treat socket as the alignment boundary instead of NUMA node |\n| `distribute-cpus-across-cores` | alpha | Prefer separate physical cores when allocating hyperthreads |\n\n### 3.6 Memory Manager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go` (Manager interface +\nmanager struct), `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy.go`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/state/`\n\nMirrors the CPU manager's design. Policies are `none` and `Static`.\n\n`Static` policy pins Guaranteed pod containers to specific NUMA memory nodes based on\ntheir `hugepages-*` and `memory` requests. The allocation is recorded in\n`{KubeletRootDir}/memory_manager_state`.\n\n`GetMemoryNUMANodes(pod, container)` returns the NUMA node set for an allocated\ncontainer. This is consumed by `InternalContainerLifecycle.PreCreateContainer()` to\nwrite `cpusetMems` into the CRI `ContainerConfig.Linux.Resources` before the container\nis created.\n\n`GetTopologyHints()` participates in the topology manager hint collection. The returned\nhints enumerate which NUMA node combinations can satisfy the container's memory and\nhugepage requests.\n\n### 3.7 Topology Manager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go` (Manager interface,\nmanager struct), `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/scope.go` (Scope interface and base\nstruct), `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/scope_container.go`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/scope_pod.go`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy*.go`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/bitmask/`\n\nThe topology manager is a **cross-resource NUMA alignment broker**. It collects\n`TopologyHint` values from all registered `HintProvider`s (CPU manager, memory\nmanager, device manager) and finds the globally optimal NUMA assignment before\nadmission proceeds.\n\n```go\ntype TopologyHint struct {\n    NUMANodeAffinity bitmask.BitMask\n    Preferred        bool\n}\n```\n\n`Manager` embeds `lifecycle.PodAdmitHandler` via `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()`.\nThe admit sequence (for `containerScope`):\n\n```\ncontainerScope.Admit(ctx, pod)\n  for each container:\n    accumulateProvidersHints()   // calls GetTopologyHints on each HintProvider\n    policy.Merge(hints)          // picks best hint\n    setTopologyHints(uid, name)  // stores result in podTopologyHints map\n    allocateAlignedResources()   // calls HintProvider.Allocate for each provider\n```\n\nAfter this, each HintProvider can call `Store.GetAffinity(podUID, containerName)` to\nretrieve the chosen NUMA mask and do its final allocation (e.g., CPU manager picks CPUs\nfrom that NUMA node, device manager picks devices on that node).\n\n**Policies**:\n\n| Name | Behaviour |\n|------|-----------|\n| `none` | No alignment; all hints ignored. Admits everything. |\n| `best-effort` | Prefers aligned hints; admits even if no aligned hint is available. |\n| `restricted` | Prefers aligned hints; rejects the pod if no aligned preferred hint exists. |\n| `single-numa-node` | Requires all resources to fit on a single NUMA node. |\n\n**Scopes**: `container` evaluates hints per container; `pod` collects hints across all\ncontainers and finds a single NUMA assignment for the whole pod.\n\nHard limit: the topology manager refuses to start on machines with more than 8 NUMA\nnodes (defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes = 8, line 41 of `topology_manager.go`), because the\nnumber of possible bitmask combinations grows exponentially.\n\n### 3.8 Device Manager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go` (ManagerImpl),\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/plugin/v1beta1/` (gRPC plugin server),\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/checkpoint/`\n\n`ManagerImpl` is the server-side of the device plugin protocol. Plugins register by\nconnecting to the kubelet's Unix socket (`pluginapi.KubeletSocket`, default\n`/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/kubelet.sock`).\n\nKey in-memory state:\n\n- `endpoints map[string]endpointInfo` \u2013 one per resource name (e.g.,\n  `\"nvidia.com/gpu\"`), keyed by resource name.\n- `allDevices ResourceDeviceInstances` \u2013 all known devices from all plugins.\n- `healthyDevices / unhealthyDevices map[string]sets.Set[string]` \u2013 health state.\n- `allocatedDevices map[string]sets.Set[string]` \u2013 per-resource allocated device IDs.\n- `podDevices *podDevices` \u2013 maps (pod, container) to allocated device IDs and their\n  run options (Devices, Mounts, Envs, Annotations).\n\n**Admission**: `UpdatePluginResources()` calls `deviceManager.UpdatePluginResources()`\nwhich invokes the plugin's `Allocate` gRPC call. The response (device nodes, bind\nmounts, environment variables, CDI annotations) is stored in `podDevices` for retrieval\nat run time.\n\n**Run time**: `GetDeviceRunContainerOptions()` is called from\n`ContainerManager.GetResources()` which is called from\n`GenerateRunContainerOptions()`. It retrieves the stored device assignments and returns\nthem as `RunContainerOptions`.\n\n**Checkpoint**: `podDevices` is serialised to a checkpoint file in `checkpointdir`\n(derived from the socket path) so allocations survive kubelet restarts.\n\n`GetTopologyHints()` returns NUMA hints based on the `Topology` field reported by the\ndevice plugin in its `ListAndWatch` response.\n\n### 3.9 DRA Manager\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`, `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/plugin/`,\n`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/state/`\n\nThe DRA manager is guarded by the `DynamicResourceAllocation` feature gate. It manages\n`ResourceClaim` objects via structured parameter drivers.\n\n**Prepare/Unprepare lifecycle**:\n\n```\nContainerManager.PrepareDynamicResources(ctx, pod)\n  \u2192 dra.Manager.PrepareResources(ctx, pod)\n    for each pod.Spec.ResourceClaims:\n      fetch ResourceClaim from API server\n      call DRAPlugin.NodePrepareResources (gRPC)\n      persist claim info to claimInfoCache\n```\n\n`UnprepareResources(ctx, pod)` calls `NodeUnprepareResources` and removes from cache.\n\nThe `reconcileLoop()` runs every 60 s (defaultReconcilePeriod). Once\n`sourcesReady.AllReady()`, it identifies pods that no longer appear in `activePods()`\nand calls `UnprepareResources` for their claims.\n\n**Plugin management** (`draplugin.DRAPluginManager`): handles plugin registration and\nderegistration events from the plugin watcher. When a plugin deregisters and does not\nre-register within `defaultWipingDelay` (30 s), the manager deletes the plugin's\n`ResourceSlice` objects from the API server.\n\nState is persisted in two files:\n- `{KubeletRootDir}/dra_manager_state` \u2013 `claimInfoCache`\n- `{KubeletRootDir}/dra_health_state` \u2013 `healthInfoCache`\n\n### 3.10 InternalContainerLifecycle\n\n**Files**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` (interface +\n`internalContainerLifecycleImpl`), `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go`\n(Linux `PreCreateContainer` override)\n\n`InternalContainerLifecycle` exposes three hooks called by the container runtime\nmanager (`pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime`):\n\n```go\ntype InternalContainerLifecycle interface {\n    PreCreateContainer(logger, pod, container, *runtimeapi.ContainerConfig) error\n    PreStartContainer(logger, pod, container, containerID string) error\n    PostStopContainer(logger, containerID string) error\n}\n```\n\n`internalContainerLifecycleImpl` holds references to `cpuManager`, `memoryManager`,\nand `topologyManager`. These are the three managers that need to act synchronously on\nindividual container events.\n\n**`PreCreateContainer`** (Linux only, `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go:31`):\nInjects CPU and memory constraints directly into the `ContainerConfig` that will be\nsent to the CRI `CreateContainer` call:\n\n```go\ncontainerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetCpus = allocatedCPUs.String()\ncontainerConfig.Linux.Resources.CpusetMems = strings.Join(affinity, \",\")\n```\n\nThis is the point where the CPU manager's `cpuset.CPUSet` assignment and the memory\nmanager's NUMA node set become concrete CRI fields that the runtime will write into\nthe container cgroup.\n\n**`PreStartContainer`** (`internal_container_lifecycle.go:41`): After the container is\ncreated but before it starts, records the `containerID \u2192 (pod, container)` mapping in\n`cpuManager.AddContainer()`, `memoryManager.AddContainer()`, and\n`topologyManager.AddContainer()`. These mappings are needed for reconciliation and\ncleanup.\n\n**`PostStopContainer`** (`internal_container_lifecycle.go:55`): Calls\n`topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)`, which removes the container from the\n`podTopologyHints` map. Note that `cpuManager.RemoveContainer` is called separately by\nthe kuberuntime layer.\n\n---\n\n## 4. End-to-End Flows\n\n### 4.1 Kubelet startup: ContainerManager.Start()\n\n`containerManagerImpl.Start()` (`container_manager_linux.go:615`) executes in strict\norder:\n\n```\n1. buildContainerMapAndRunningSetFromRuntime(ctx, runtimeService)\n       Lists all pod sandboxes and containers via CRI.\n       Produces containerMap (pod\u2192container\u2192containerID) and runningSet.\n\n2. draManager.Start(ctx, activePods, getNode, sourcesReady)   [if DRA enabled]\n       Starts the DRA plugin manager and reconcile goroutine.\n\n3. cpuManager.Start(ctx, activePods, sourcesReady, \u2026, containerMap.Clone())\n       Reads/writes cpu_manager_state checkpoint.\n       policy.Start() removes stale assignments.\n       Starts reconcile goroutine.\n\n4. memoryManager.Start(ctx, activePods, sourcesReady, \u2026, containerMap.Clone())\n       Reads/writes memory_manager_state checkpoint.\n       policy.Start() removes stale assignments.\n\n5. Cache node info; optionally add rootfs capacity.\n\n6. validateNodeAllocatable()\n       Fails if reservations exceed capacity.\n\n7. setupNode(ctx, activePods)\n       validateSystemRequirements() + setupKernelTunables()\n       createNodeAllocatableCgroups()   \u2192 creates kubepods cgroup\n       qosContainerManager.Start()      \u2192 creates burstable/besteffort cgroups\n       enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()  \u2192 writes kubepods resource limits (with retry)\n       Optionally place kubelet in KubeletCgroupsName cgroup.\n\n8. Start systemContainer state-ensure goroutine (every 1 min)\n\n9. Start periodicTasks goroutine (every 5 min)\n       Used to discover kubelet's own cgroup when KubeletCgroupsName is empty.\n\n10. deviceManager.Start(logger, activePods, sourcesReady, containerMap, runningSet)\n        Reads device plugin checkpoint.\n        Starts gRPC plugin server.\n        Reconciles existing containers.\n```\n\nIf any step fails, `Start()` returns an error and the kubelet exits (line 1754 of\n`kubelet.go`).\n\n### 4.2 Pod admission\n\nAdmission handlers are chained in `kubelet.go` around line 1064:\n\n```\nGetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()  \u2192 topologyManager (implements PodAdmitHandler)\nNewPredicateAdmitHandler(\u2026, UpdatePluginResources)  \u2192 device plugin Allocate\n```\n\n**Topology manager admit** (`topologymanager/scope_container.go:49`):\n\n```\nfor each container in pod (init + regular):\n    accumulateProvidersHints()    // GetTopologyHints from cpuManager, memManager, deviceManager\n    policy.Merge(providersHints)  // find best NUMA bitmask\n    setTopologyHints(uid, name)   // store chosen hint\n    allocateAlignedResources()\n      for each hintProvider:\n        hintProvider.Allocate(pod, container)\n          cpuManager.Allocate()    \u2192 policy.Allocate() \u2192 writes to state\n          memoryManager.Allocate() \u2192 policy.Allocate() \u2192 writes to state\n          deviceManager.Allocate() [via GetDeviceRunContainerOptions at run-time]\n```\n\nIf the chosen hint is not `Preferred` and the policy is `restricted` or\n`single-numa-node`, the pod is rejected with a `TopologyAffinityError` and a\n`TopologyAffinityError` event reason.\n\n**Device plugin admit** (`UpdatePluginResources`): calls `Allocate` on each device\nplugin that has resources requested by the pod. If this returns an error, the pod is\nrejected.\n\nAfter admission the pod's resource allocations are fully committed in the in-memory\nand on-disk state of each sub-manager. Failure at a later step (cgroup creation, CRI\ncall) does not automatically undo these allocations; they are cleaned up on the\nsubsequent `RemoveContainer` / pod teardown path.\n\n### 4.3 Pod creation: syncPod\n\nWithin `syncPod` the container manager is involved at several points:\n\n1. **DRA preparation** (`PrepareDynamicResources`, `kubelet.go:3310`): Calls\n   `dra.Manager.PrepareResources()`. The DRA driver's `NodePrepareResources` gRPC\n   response returns CDI device annotations that are included in the CRI\n   `RunPodSandbox` call.\n\n2. **Pod cgroup creation** (`podContainerManagerImpl.EnsureExists()`):\n   Called from kubelet pod workers. Creates `kubepods/{qos}/pod<UID>` cgroup with\n   resource limits from `ResourceConfigForPod()`.\n\n3. **QoS cgroup update** (`UpdateQOSCgroups()`): Recalculates `kubepods/burstable`\n   CPU shares to account for the newly scheduled pod.\n\n4. **Container run options** (`GetResources()`): For each container, assembles\n   `RunContainerOptions.Devices`, `.Mounts`, `.Envs`, `.Annotations` from the device\n   manager (and DRA manager, if enabled). These become fields in the CRI\n   `CreateContainerRequest`.\n\n5. **`PreCreateContainer` hook**: CPU manager's cpuset and memory manager's NUMA node\n   set are injected into `ContainerConfig.Linux.Resources` before the CRI call.\n\n6. **`PreStartContainer` hook**: After `CreateContainer` succeeds, container ID\n   mappings are recorded in all three hook-aware managers.\n\n### 4.4 Container start: InternalContainerLifecycle hooks\n\nCall site (kuberuntime layer, `pkg/kubelet/kuberuntime/kuberuntime_container.go`):\n\n```\n// Before CRI CreateContainer:\nlifecycle.PreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n\n// After CRI CreateContainer, before CRI StartContainer:\nlifecycle.PreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n\n// After CRI StopContainer:\nlifecycle.PostStopContainer(containerID)\n```\n\n`PreCreateContainer` is where the CPU manager's exclusive cpuset and the memory\nmanager's NUMA memory node assignment enter the CRI flow. If the CPU manager has no\nallocation for this container (none policy, or burstable/best-effort container under\nthe static policy), `allocatedCPUs.IsEmpty()` is true and `CpusetCpus` is left\nunset (the runtime inherits the shared cpuset from the pod cgroup).\n\n### 4.5 Container stop and pod teardown\n\n```\n1. lifecycle.PostStopContainer(containerID)\n       topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n\n2. cpuManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)   [called by kuberuntime]\n       policy.RemoveContainer() \u2192 returns CPUs to shared pool\n       updates cpu_manager_state checkpoint\n\n3. memoryManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n       policy.RemoveContainer() \u2192 returns NUMA memory blocks\n       updates memory_manager_state checkpoint\n\n4. PodContainerManager.ReduceCPULimits()  [before cgroup destroy]\n5. PodContainerManager.tryKillingCgroupProcesses()\n6. PodContainerManager.Destroy()  \u2192 cgroupManager.Destroy()\n\n7. dra.Manager.UnprepareResources(ctx, pod)  [if DRA claims exist]\n       NodeUnprepareResources gRPC call\n       removes from claimInfoCache\n```\n\n### 4.6 Sub-manager reconcile loops\n\n| Manager | Period | Purpose |\n|---------|--------|---------|\n| CPU manager `reconcileState` | `CPUManagerReconcilePeriod` (default 10 s) | Re-writes cpuset to CRI for all running containers; catches divergence after restart |\n| QoS container manager `UpdateCgroups` | 1 minute (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`) | Re-calculates burstable CPU shares and optional memory reservation |\n| Device manager | event-driven | Plugin health updates trigger `resourceupdates.Update` on `cm.resourceUpdates` channel |\n| DRA manager `reconcileLoop` | 60 s (`defaultReconcilePeriod`) | Unprepares claims for pods that are no longer active |\n| `systemContainers` goroutine | 1 minute | Ensures system cgroups (kubelet, OS services) are correctly bounded |\n| `periodicTasks` goroutine | 5 minutes | Discovers kubelet's own cgroup if `KubeletCgroupsName` is empty |\n\nThe `cm.resourceUpdates` channel (capacity 10, created at\n`container_manager_linux.go:360`) aggregates `resourceupdates.Update` messages from\ndevice manager and (when `ResourceHealthStatus` is enabled) from the DRA manager. The\nkubelet main loop reads from this channel at line 2669 of `kubelet.go` to trigger\nstatus re-sync for pods whose device health changed.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Cgroup Hierarchy\n\n### 5.1 Name abstraction and driver translation\n\n`CgroupName` (`types.go:49`) is `[]string` \u2013 an abstract component list. The concrete\nfilesystem path depends on the cgroup driver:\n\n| Driver | Conversion | Example input | Example output |\n|--------|-----------|---------------|----------------|\n| cgroupfs | `CgroupName.ToCgroupfs()` | `{\"kubepods\",\"burstable\",\"podabc\"}` | `/kubepods/burstable/podabc` |\n| systemd | `CgroupName.ToSystemd()` | `{\"kubepods\",\"burstable\",\"podabc\"}` | `/kubepods.slice/kubepods-burstable.slice/kubepods-burstable-podabc.slice` |\n\nThe systemd conversion (`cgroup_manager_linux.go:81`) calls\n`cgroupsystemd.ExpandSlice()` from `opencontainers/cgroups`. The `-` character in a\nCgroupName component is mapped to `_` (and back) to allow unambiguous round-tripping,\nwhich is why `_` is forbidden in cgroup name components (enforced with a panic in\n`NewCgroupName()`).\n\n### 5.2 Cgroup v1 vs. cgroup v2\n\nUnder cgroup v1, each resource controller has its own subtree. The kubelet mounts are\ndiscovered via `GetCgroupSubsystems()` which reads `/proc/mounts`. The allowlisted\ncontrollers are: `cpu`, `cpuacct`, `cpuset`, `memory`, `systemd`, `pids` (plus\n`hugetlb` if present). A cgroup is considered to `Exist` if all allowed controller\npaths exist on disk (`cgroupV1impl.Validate()`).\n\nUnder cgroup v2, a single unified hierarchy lives at `/sys/fs/cgroup`. A cgroup exists\nif its directory exists and the necessary controllers are listed in\n`cgroup.controllers`. The `cgroupV2impl.Validate()` method reads\n`cgroup.subtree_control` to check controller availability.\n\nCgroup v1 support is deprecated as of this release:\n\n```go\n// pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go:52\nCgroupV1DeprecatedWarning = \"cgroup v1 detected. cgroup v1 support is deprecated \u2026\"\n```\n\nThe kubelet logs this warning at startup if `/sys/fs/cgroup` is not in unified mode.\n\n### 5.3 The four-tier tree\n\n```\n/\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 kubepods/                    \u2190 cgroupRoot (\"kubepods\")\n    \u2502                              limits = Node Allocatable\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 (no subdir)               \u2190 Guaranteed pod cgroups live here\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 pod<UID>/\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 <container-cgroup>  (managed by CRI/runtime)\n    \u2502\n    \u251c\u2500\u2500 burstable/               \u2190 kubepods/burstable\n    \u2502   \u2502                          cpu.shares = \u2211(burstable pod CPU requests)\n    \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 pod<UID>/\n    \u2502       \u2514\u2500\u2500 <container-cgroup>\n    \u2502\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 besteffort/              \u2190 kubepods/besteffort\n        \u2502                          cpu.shares = MinShares (2)\n        \u2514\u2500\u2500 pod<UID>/\n            \u2514\u2500\u2500 <container-cgroup>\n```\n\nContainer cgroups inside each pod cgroup are created and managed by the container\nruntime (containerd, CRI-O). The kubelet's container manager does not create them;\nit only creates the `kubepods`, `burstable`, `besteffort`, and `pod<UID>` cgroups.\n\nThe CRI `CreateContainer` request carries the pod's cgroup parent path via the\n`linux.cgroup_parent` field. The kubelet sets this to the cgroupfs path returned by\n`GetPodCgroupRoot()` / `GetPodContainerName()`.\n\n---\n\n## 6. State Persistence\n\nAll sub-managers that own exclusive resource assignments checkpoint their state into\nfiles under `{KubeletRootDir}` (default `/var/lib/kubelet`):\n\n| File | Owner | Format |\n|------|-------|--------|\n| `cpu_manager_state` | CPU manager | JSON: policy name + `ContainerCPUAssignments` map |\n| `memory_manager_state` | Memory manager | JSON: memory blocks per (pod, container) |\n| `dra_manager_state` | DRA manager | JSON: claim info cache |\n| `dra_health_state` | DRA manager | JSON: device health info |\n| `device-plugins/kubelet_internal_checkpoint` | Device manager | JSON: pod\u2192container\u2192device allocation |\n\nOn kubelet restart, each manager reads back its checkpoint file and reconciles the\nstored assignments against the containers reported by the CRI. Entries with no matching\ncontainer are considered stale and freed.\n\nFor the CPU manager, if the checkpoint was written by a different policy name, startup\nis aborted and the operator must drain the node and delete `cpu_manager_state`. This\nprevents silent CPU over-subscription that would occur if `static` assignments were\nloaded back while the `none` policy is active.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Failure Modes and Tradeoffs\n\n### Node allocatable enforcement retry loop\n\n`enforceNodeAllocatableCgroups()` spins in a goroutine retrying every minute when it\ncannot write the memory limit to `kubepods`. This can happen when existing pod memory\nusage already exceeds the new limit. Until the retry succeeds, the cgroup limit is not\nenforced and pods can consume more memory than the administrator intended.\n\n**Implication**: When lowering reservations (e.g., increasing kubeReserved) on a live\nnode, eviction must happen first. The retry loop does not trigger eviction \u2013 that is\nhandled by the eviction manager separately. An operator who reduces `--kube-reserved`\nmemory without an intervening drain may see warning events for an extended period.\n\n### CPU manager static policy and shared pool starvation\n\nThe shared pool consists of CPUs not pinned to any exclusive container. If a large\nnumber of Guaranteed containers with exclusive CPUs are running, the shared pool can\nshrink to the reserved CPUs only. At that point, new containers that need to run from\nthe shared pool will still start (the kubelet does not gate on shared pool size), but\ntheir available CPU time is reduced to what the reserved CPUs can provide plus the\nweighted CFS shares.\n\nWith `strict-cpu-reservation=true`, reserved CPUs are completely removed from the\nshared pool and assigned only to system/kubelet use. This ensures isolation but shrinks\nthe pool further.\n\n### Topology manager NUMA node limit\n\nThe hard ceiling of 8 NUMA nodes (`defaultMaxAllowableNUMANodes`) means the topology\nmanager cannot start on machines with more nodes (e.g., large AMD EPYC servers may\nhave 16+ NUMA nodes). On such machines `TopologyManagerPolicy` must be set to `none`.\n\n### QoS CPU share staleness\n\nThe burstable cgroup's `cpu.shares` value is recomputed from active pod CPU requests\nonce per minute and during each `syncPod`. Between updates, if pods are added or\nremoved quickly, the shares value may be transiently incorrect. In practice this affects\nscheduling fairness during bursty workloads rather than causing hard failures.\n\n### Memory manager static policy and fragmentation\n\nThe memory manager allocates NUMA memory blocks in units defined by the machine's\nmemory topology. Fragmentation can prevent a new Guaranteed pod from being admitted\neven if there is enough total free memory across NUMA nodes, because the policy\nrequires contiguous NUMA-local allocation. The pod will be rejected with an\n`UnexpectedAdmissionError` type.\n\n### Device plugin checkpoint and restart\n\nThe device plugin checkpoint stores pod\u2192device assignments. If the checkpoint is lost\n(e.g., disk failure) and the kubelet restarts while device-using pods are running,\nthe kubelet will re-admit the pods and attempt re-allocation. Depending on device\nplugin behaviour, this may fail or result in double-allocation until the plugin\nreconciles its own state.\n\n### DRA wipe delay race\n\nWhen a DRA driver restarts, there is a 30-second window (`defaultWipingDelay`) before\nthe DRA manager deletes its `ResourceSlice` objects. If the driver does not re-register\nwithin this window, the scheduler will stop using the node's slices. Setting this\nwindow too short increases the risk of unnecessary slice deletion; too long leaves\nstale resource advertisement on the node.\n\n### cgroup v2 MemoryQoS and `memory.min`\n\nThe `memory.min` value written by `setMemoryQoS()` represents the sum of memory\nrequests for pods in each QoS tier. If a process outside the kubepods cgroup consumes\nmemory, the kernel may OOM-kill processes in cgroups without `memory.min` protection\nbefore reclaiming from cgroups that have it. This is the intended behaviour (Guaranteed\npods are protected), but it means BestEffort pods can be killed even when free memory\nis nominally available.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Extension Points\n\n### Adding a new CPU manager policy\n\nImplement the `Policy` interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go`):\n\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Name() string\n    Start(logger logr.Logger, s state.State) error\n    Allocate(logger logr.Logger, s state.State, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n    RemoveContainer(logger logr.Logger, s state.State, podUID string, containerName string) error\n    GetTopologyHints(*v1.Pod, *v1.Container) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetPodTopologyHints(*v1.Pod) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetAllocatableCPUs(s state.State) cpuset.CPUSet\n}\n```\n\nRegister the new policy by adding a case in the `switch` statement in\n`NewManager()` (`cpu_manager.go:172`).\n\n### Adding a new memory manager policy\n\nImplement the `Policy` interface (`pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy.go`):\n\n```go\ntype Policy interface {\n    Name() string\n    Start(logger klog.Logger, s state.State) error\n    Allocate(logger klog.Logger, s state.State, pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n    RemoveContainer(logger klog.Logger, s state.State, podUID string, containerName string)\n    GetTopologyHints(\u2026) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetPodTopologyHints(\u2026) map[string][]topologymanager.TopologyHint\n    GetAllocatableMemory(s state.State) []state.Block\n}\n```\n\nAdd a case in `NewManager()` (`memory_manager.go:138`).\n\n### Adding a topology manager hint provider\n\nAny subsystem that wants to participate in NUMA alignment must implement\n`topologymanager.HintProvider`:\n\n```go\ntype HintProvider interface {\n    GetTopologyHints(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) map[string][]TopologyHint\n    GetPodTopologyHints(pod *v1.Pod) map[string][]TopologyHint\n    Allocate(pod *v1.Pod, container *v1.Container) error\n}\n```\n\nRegister by calling `topologyManager.AddHintProvider(logger, provider)` in\n`NewContainerManager()`. The topology manager will call `GetTopologyHints()` during\nadmission and `Allocate()` after the best hint is chosen.\n\n### Adding a device plugin resource\n\nDevice plugins are out-of-tree by design. A new plugin:\n1. Creates a Unix socket under `/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`.\n2. Implements the `DevicePlugin` gRPC service defined in\n   `k8s.io/kubelet/pkg/apis/deviceplugin/v1beta1`.\n3. Registers with the kubelet by calling `Register()` on the kubelet socket.\n\nThe plugin watcher (`pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager`) discovers the socket and calls the\ndevice manager's registration handler via `GetPluginRegistrationHandlers()`.\n\n### Adding a DRA driver\n\nDRA drivers implement `k8s.io/kubelet/pkg/apis/dra/v1.DRAPluginServer` gRPC service\n(primarily `NodePrepareResources` and `NodeUnprepareResources`). They register through\nthe same plugin watcher mechanism, using the `DRAPlugin` registration type.\n\n### Replacing the CgroupManager\n\n`CgroupManager` is an interface (`types.go:64`). Tests and non-standard builds can\nsubstitute any implementation. In-tree there is a fake in `pkg/kubelet/cm/testing/`.\nProvide a new implementation and pass it through `NewContainerManager`'s dependency\ninjection path (currently hardcoded in `container_manager_linux.go`'s local\n`NewCgroupManager()` call) or inject via a test shim.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Platform Variants\n\n| File | Build constraint | Behaviour |\n|------|-----------------|-----------|\n| `container_manager_linux.go` | `linux` | Full implementation: cgroups, QoS, CPU/memory/device/DRA/topology managers |\n| `container_manager_windows.go` | `windows` | Device manager always enabled; CPU and memory managers enabled only with `WindowsCPUAndMemoryAffinity` feature gate; no cgroup hierarchy |\n| `container_manager_stub.go` | (none \u2013 always compiled) | No-op for testing; used by `NewStubContainerManager()` |\n| `container_manager_unsupported.go` | `!linux && !windows` | `Start()` always returns an error |\n| `cgroup_manager_unsupported.go` | `!linux` | `GetCgroupSubsystems()` returns empty |\n| `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go` | `linux` | `PreCreateContainer()` injects cpuset/cpusetMems |\n| `internal_container_lifecycle_windows.go` | `windows` | No-op `PreCreateContainer()` |\n| `internal_container_lifecycle_unsupported.go` | `!linux && !windows` | No-op `PreCreateContainer()` |\n| `node_container_manager_linux.go` | `linux` | Node Allocatable cgroup enforcement |\n| `qos_container_manager_linux.go` | (package cm, imported on linux only indirectly) | QoS cgroup tiers |\n| `pod_container_manager_linux.go` | (package cm, linux) | Pod cgroup creation |\n| `helpers_linux.go` | `linux` | CPU/memory arithmetic, cgroup subsystem discovery |\n| `helpers_unsupported.go` | `!linux` | Stub helpers that return zeros |\n\nThe Windows implementation uses a fake topology manager (`topologymanager.NewFakeManager()`),\na fake CPU manager (`cpumanager.NewFakeManager()`), and a fake memory manager\n(`memorymanager.NewFakeManager()`) unless `WindowsCPUAndMemoryAffinity` is explicitly\nenabled, at which point the real managers are constructed (container_manager_windows.go\nlines 143\u2013187).\n\n---\n\n## 10.
